<div id="review_503836206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/503836206" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/503836206?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Hardcore Batman fans!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=modern-age-comics">modern-age-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=sexy-bad-boy-hero">sexy-bad-boy-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-hero">strong-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=dc-comics">dc-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=jeph-loeb">jeph-loeb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer503836206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8466503938365703299"><b>
  <u>The Origins of Harvey Dent has begun!</u>
</b><br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404772i/787964._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='400' alt='Two Face' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>
  <u>Introduction:</u>
</b> <br/><br/>Now, I have been reading many Batman comics whose stories dealt with Batman defeating one of his greatest foes, the Joker. But, I had always wanted to read some “Batman” stories that dealt with another one of Batman’s greatest foes, Two-Face! I got interested in Two-Face’s story when I saw one of the episodes on “Batman: The Animated Series” that dealt with the origin tale of Two-Face and I was amazed at how well that episode portrayed</span>
  <span id="freeText8466503938365703299" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>The Origins of Harvey Dent has begun!</u>
</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404772i/787964._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="Two Face" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <u>Introduction:</u>
</b> <br><br>Now, I have been reading many Batman comics whose stories dealt with Batman defeating one of his greatest foes, the Joker. But, I had always wanted to read some “Batman” stories that dealt with another one of Batman’s greatest foes, Two-Face! I got interested in Two-Face’s story when I saw one of the episodes on “Batman: The Animated Series” that dealt with the origin tale of Two-Face and I was amazed at how well that episode portrayed the relationship between Batman and Two-Face. So, this caused me to pick up a Batman comic book that deals with Two-Face and lo and behold, I found “Batman: The Long Halloween!”<br><br><b>
  <u>What is this story about?</u>
</b><br><br>Carmine “The Roman” Falcone was Gotham City’s untouchable Crime Lord and District Attorney, Harvey Dent, Batman and Captain James Gordon were all trying to take down this crime lord for months now. However, the actual story starts when “The Roman” was throwing a wedding party for his nephew Johnny Viti, but later on, it turns out that somebody had murdered Johnny Viti and later on, a gang called “The Irish.” This then leads to many murders that are directly involved with “The Roman’s” family and the serial killer became known as “Holiday” since the killer only kills people on various holidays such as Thanksgiving and Christmas. Can Batman, James Gordon and Harvey Dent catch this serial killer before it is too late?<br><br><b>
  <u>What I loved about this story:</u>
</b><br><br><u>Jeph Loeb’s writing:</u> Now, I had seen many different versions of Harvey Dent’s origins including the animated series’ version and Nolan’s famous “Batman” film, “The Dark Knight,” but I really enjoyed Jeph Loeb’s version of Harvey Dent and how he made his character mysterious. Jeph Loeb had done an excellent job at writing this story as the serial killer starts killing certain members of “The Roman’s” family on holidays such as Halloween, Thanksgiving, Christmas and New Year’s Eve and I loved how all thirteen chapters in this book is titled a different holiday like Chapter Two is titled “Thanksgiving” and Chapter Three is titled “Christmas.” I also loved the way that Jeph Loeb made this story similar to a crime noir as the mystery of the story involves Batman, Harvey Dent and James Gordon trying to figure out who the “Holiday” serial killer is and how they will stop him from killing anymore victims and I loved seeing the scenes of the “Holiday” serial killer murdering people as there are no words accompanying the evil deeds and the artwork pretty much does the talking for those scenes. I really enjoyed the turbulent relationship between Catwoman and Batman as we are left in the dark about Catwoman’s true motives for helping out Batman even though she is a world class burglar and it was interesting trying to figure out what her true motives are. The way that Jeph Loeb portrayed Harvey Dent’s mysterious and intense character was extremely well done as Harvey Dent also wants to protect Gotham City from crime, but he seems to want to do things the hard way to get the job done. What was so amazing about this story was the fact that Jeph Loeb introduced many of Batman’s greatest enemies (the Joker, Solomon Grundy, Poison Ivy, The Scarecrow, and the Mad Hatter) into this one story and they all play a huge role in Batman trying to discover “Holiday’s” secret identity.<br><br><u>Tim Sale’s artwork:</u> Tim Sale’s artwork in this graphic novel was just astonishing as the artwork is dark and gritty and it really fits well with the dark tone of this story! I loved the way that Tim Sale drew Batman himself as Batman looks large and intimidating in every image and I loved the way that Tim Sale drew Batman’s cape as twirling around Batman, giving a frightening feel to Batman’s presence. I also loved the way that Tim Sale drew the shadowing around the characters’ bodies during the night scenes (although the majority of this comic takes place at night) which really made the images extremely creepy to look at. What I really loved about Tim Sale’s artwork is when the scenes of “Holiday” murdering various victims are in black and white colorings which really made these scenes truly stand out from the other scenes.<br><br><b>
  <u>What made me feel uncomfortable about this story:</u>
</b><br><br>Since this story deals with the murders of several characters, there are many scenes where characters are killed off in gruesome ways, which they are mainly shot in the head. These scenes are also graphic as there is blood everywhere where the characters are shot. Anyone who is uncomfortable with violence in graphic novels might want to steer away from this graphic novel. Also, there is some brief language in this graphic novel, although the language is not as strong as you would sometimes see in mature stories<br><br><b>
  <u>Final Thoughts:</u>
</b><br><br>Overall, “Batman: The Long Halloween” is one of the best “Batman” stories about Two-Face ever told and anyone who is a fan of the “Batman” comics should definitely check this graphic novel out! Also, if you want to read some other great “Batman” comics, here are some recommendations:<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59980.Batman_Year_One" title="Batman Year One by Frank Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">Batman: Year One</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/96358.Batman_The_Killing_Joke" title="Batman The Killing Joke by Alan Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">Batman: The Killing Joke</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59960.Batman_The_Dark_Knight_Returns" title="Batman The Dark Knight Returns by Frank Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">Batman: The Dark Knight Returns</a><br><br><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2013/01/batman-long-halloween-by-jeph-loeb.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8466503938365703299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1630983188" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630983188" />
    <a title="Jeannette Nikolova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2574284-jeannette-nikolova"><img alt="Jeannette Nikolova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480677087p2/2574284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1630983188?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeannette Nikolova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeannette Nikolova" href="/user/show/2574284-jeannette-nikolova">Jeannette Nikolova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1630983188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17242916398496424861"><a href='https://wondrousbooks.wordpress.com/2016/05/18/batman-the-long-halloween-by-jeph-loeb/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Also available on the WondrousBooks blog.</i>
</a><br/><br/><br/>I can't say that I had fun reading <strong>The Long Halloween</strong>. Rather, I grew tired with it by the end. It's okay, of course, because luckily authors and illustrators of comic books change all the time, but as praised as this book is by critics and fans alike, it was not for me. Both the story and the art were more old school that I was in for. On the other hand, with time and reading more Batman, I think I might revisit it and maybe even have a new appreciat</span>
  <span id="freeText17242916398496424861" style="display:none"><a href="https://wondrousbooks.wordpress.com/2016/05/18/batman-the-long-halloween-by-jeph-loeb/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Also available on the WondrousBooks blog.</i>
</a><br /><br /><br />I can't say that I had fun reading <strong>The Long Halloween</strong>. Rather, I grew tired with it by the end. It's okay, of course, because luckily authors and illustrators of comic books change all the time, but as praised as this book is by critics and fans alike, it was not for me. Both the story and the art were more old school that I was in for. On the other hand, with time and reading more Batman, I think I might revisit it and maybe even have a new appreciation for it.<br /><br />I liked the mixed batch of villains and the cameos and name-dropping, but ultimately, the story was based around the <em>Holiday</em> killer and that in the end turned out underwhelming for me.<br /><br />Also, as it was old fashioned, both in terms of how it was written and what was included in it, I felt it lacked juice and was very schematic and almost following a pattern which became tiring and predictable after a while.<br /><br /><strong>Most of all, I disliked Batman himself</strong>. There was nothing too personal about him, he was like a winged automaton the struggles of whom did not interest me at all. The most private remark that was made by his own narration was "I believe in Jim Gordon/Gotham/Harvey Dent." He was way too remote for me as a human being, most of all, and that is what is supposed to draw the reader to Batman, who is just a man, after all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17242916398496424861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2573008580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2573008580" />
    <a title="Britton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/86934326-britton"><img alt="Britton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547147480p2/86934326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2573008580?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Britton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Britton" href="/user/show/86934326-britton">Britton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=political-politics">political-politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=crime-noir-hardboiled-mystery">crime-noir-hardboiled-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=books-you-should-really-check-out">books-you-should-really-check-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=amazing-authors">amazing-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=dc-comics">dc-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=books-i-ve-read-multiple-times">books-i-ve-read-multiple-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=action-thriller-adventure">action-thriller-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2573008580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12581895127752320594">"I believe in Harvey Dent." <br/><br/>Belief is all that we have in this world. Gilda states her belief in her husband Harvey Dent, Gordon states his belief in law and order, and of this city, but most importantly Batman states his belief in Harvey Dent, his city, alongside his crusade. Batman's whole crusade is based in the belief that one man can eradicate crime, and it is his obsession with eradicating crime that drives, as well as his belief in his cause. If anything, it shows that if we didn't have b</span>
  <span id="freeText12581895127752320594" style="display:none">"I believe in Harvey Dent." <br /><br />Belief is all that we have in this world. Gilda states her belief in her husband Harvey Dent, Gordon states his belief in law and order, and of this city, but most importantly Batman states his belief in Harvey Dent, his city, alongside his crusade. Batman's whole crusade is based in the belief that one man can eradicate crime, and it is his obsession with eradicating crime that drives, as well as his belief in his cause. If anything, it shows that if we didn't have belief, that we would go mad, <br /><br />Being a big Batman fan, friends of mine often ask me what Batman stories that I would recommend to newcomers, it can be a complicated answer since Batman has had plenty of excellent stories over the years. I could mention Alan Moore's seminal work <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2534371527" rel="nofollow noopener">Batman: The Killing Joke</a>, or Frank Miller's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2534371469" rel="nofollow noopener">Batman: Year One</a> (which I far prefer over his much lauded The Dark Knight Returns), or Grant Morrison's remarkably odd <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2534771329" rel="nofollow noopener">Arkham Asylum: A Serious House on Serious Earth</a>. I could also mention Brian Azzerello and Lee Bermejo's Joker (though I guess that's not really a Batman story, is it?) or Scott Snyder's run on the character and so many others, but an easy choice for recommendation is always Loeb and Sale's The Long Halloween. <br /><br />To call this comic a good Batman comic is too faint a praise for this book, it is good crime fiction. Loeb and Sale have a grasp on the crime genre that are replicated by few other creative duos. I could certainly make the argument that Ed Brubaker and Sean Phillips are far more inventive with the genre, but Loeb and Sale come close in terms of the closeness of their working relationship. Many people have noticed over the years that The Long Halloween has notable similarities with Francis Ford Coppola's crime epic The Godfather, and I can certainly see that from certain lines in the book to the shadowy, gothic atmosphere that pervades both works. I'll quote my good friend Alan on this one and say that they both take a sip from the same creative well. It is funny how The Long Halloween was influenced by cinema, as The Long Halloween has been cited by Christopher Nolan as a seminal influence on his own Dark Knight trilogy and has been cited by Nolan as one of his favorite Batman stories, though sadly Nolan didn't lean into the detective aspect of Batman's character as much, though Matt Reeves seems to have taken a note from this with his new Batman adaptation, which I anxiously await. <br /><br />What makes The Long Halloween so inventive is its take on the criminal underworld, and its exploration of how normal criminals such as Carmine Falcone or Sal Maroni would react to new 'super criminals.' The way that Loeb builds tension throughout the story of the comic proves just how great of a writer that he can be. He also takes a note from Frank Miller's Year One and makes Gotham City into a more realistic, grounded city, while also never failing to capture the theatrics of the Batman mythos, creating a careful balance between these two tones that keeps The Long Halloween from faltering entirely, though sometimes Loeb can get lost with one tone over another. Much of the tension from the series shows how these super criminals begin to drive Gotham into a further state of insanity, and how Batman's appearance has now attracted more insanity to Gotham, rather than giving Gotham a sense of hope in order to end their state of constant misery and struggle. <br /><br />Much of the tragedy of the book comes from the fall of Harvey Dent, who gradually begins to lose his mind from the stress of the case of the Holiday Killer, the tensions at his home, as well as his burgeoning obsession to take down the Falcone/Maroni crime syndicate, which eventually leads to his transformation into Two Face. Much of the tension that is built throughout the story, asides from the criminals and the so called 'freaks' who are now running amok in Gotham is Harvey's deteriorating sanity and once he's doused with the acid at the trial, it's a breaking point for Harvey that he can never come back from. <br /><br />Tim Sale once again manages to show himself as one of the best artists in modern comics with this book, bringing a pulpy, yet also gothic tone not unlike one of my other favorite artists Mike Mignola of Hellboy fame. While I do have issues with Sale's body autotomy at times, I do think his idiosyncratic flare continues to have me intrigued and bares comparison to few others like Mignola, Steve Ditko, and Gabriel Ba. His style remains evocative and moody throughout the run of the series, he never gets too wacky and keeps you immersed in the tone and atmosphere of the series. It just shows the power of an inspired artist. <br /><br />Of course, there are issues that pervade throughout the book. Loeb has a knack for filibustering characters into his books when unsure how to keep the story moving along, it's not as bad as in some of his other works and it mostly works, it does rear its head at times in ways that I felt was unsatisfactory, his depiction of Scarecrow and Mad Hatter, especially when they team up is also lacking, he basically makes them into bumbling, nursury rhyme quoting buffoons, and as someone who really likes Scarecrow that was quite disappointing to see. Sale's design of the Joker is also odd, with his body autotomy occasionally reminding me of my least favorite comics artist Rob Liefeld, and also the story in that issue is lacking, while not horrible, it feels a bit out of place in this mostly serious, grounded story. The final twist is also lacking, while it works thematically in exploring how this new age of Gotham has driven its residents mad alongside the 'super villains' and our heroes, it doesn't quite work when put under intense scrutiny, which leaves me to believe that Jeph Loeb doesn't always know how to wrap up his stories, like with Ken Levine, he relies more on twists that make the story more complicated than a more natural conclusion, nevertheless, most of these complaints are mere small gripes in comparison to the heaps of praise I level at this series. <br /><br />In the end, The Long Halloween showcases the excellence that we can get when we get a writer and artist duo who are profoundly good at their crafts, and both compliment each other beautifully.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12581895127752320594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1794828755" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14029598345298843257">Accidentally, I finished <i>Dark Victory</i> before I could manage to get my hands on <i>Batman: Long Halloween</i>, I knew how this long series is going to end before I started on <i>Long Halloween</i>, still I enjoy both volumes <b>SO DAMN MUCH!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494946942ra/22770164.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>(Link: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://nerdlush.com/category/events/'>https://nerdlush.com/category/events/</a>)<br/><br/>The strongest points of <i>Long Halloween</i> and its sequel are the gloomy yet flawlessly gorgeous artwork, the strong <i>crime-noir</i> atmosphere which is shaped into perfection, the ill-fated romance between Batman and Catwoman and the use of</span>
  <span id="freeText14029598345298843257" style="display:none">Accidentally, I finished <i>Dark Victory</i> before I could manage to get my hands on <i>Batman: Long Halloween</i>, I knew how this long series is going to end before I started on <i>Long Halloween</i>, still I enjoy both volumes <b>SO DAMN MUCH!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494946942ra/22770164.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://nerdlush.com/category/events/">https://nerdlush.com/category/events/</a>)<br><br>The strongest points of <i>Long Halloween</i> and its sequel are the gloomy yet flawlessly gorgeous artwork, the strong <i>crime-noir</i> atmosphere which is shaped into perfection, the ill-fated romance between Batman and Catwoman and the use of a colorful bunch of Batman's villains: the Joker (and his huge mouth!), Poison Ivy (she is beautifully drawn), Mad Hatter, the Riddler, Scarecrow (he always has a grand entrance) and the vicious old fashion-looking Italian crime families! *What more can I ask for?*<br><br> However, comparing with <i>Dark Victory</i>, the plots and the murder mystery within <i>Long Halloween</i> is a bit weak: so there is a serial killer named 'Holiday' who is murdering the criminals within Gotham City? And this 'Holiday' mostly targets people who are tied to the most powerful crime family led by the untouchable crime lord nick-named 'The Roman'? Who is Holiday and what is he/she trying to prove by gunning down criminals during each holiday (started from Halloween)? Can Holiday actually be Harvey Dent, an ally of Batman?<br><br>The murder mystery is truly intriguing, at first; but at the end I got confused and the revealing part of the murderer's true identity a bit underwhelming: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[so the supposed dead son of 'The Roman' is Holiday, at the same time Harvey Dent and his beloved wife are also Holiday? I can understand to a degree but at the same time, I don't understand why 'The Roman's own son would want to kill his father's men and his allies <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>Anyway, this volume is still rated so, so high at my best American comics list.<br><br>Review: Red Hood: Outlaw vol. 1 <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2820609968?utm_medium=email&amp;utm_source=rating">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br>Review: Batman: Battle For the Cowl: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1794817074?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br>Review: Batman: Life After Death: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1791095500">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br>Review: Batman &amp; Robin: Batman Reborn <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2081110052?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br>Book Review: Batman: The Long Halloween <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1794828755?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br>Review: The Greatest Batman Stories Ever Told Vol. 1 (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2732359673">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>)</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_229418101" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229418101" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229418101?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=superhumans">superhumans</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229418101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13240873027633303724">The Long Halloween is a follow-up to Year One, written by Jeph Loeb because Frank Miller had no apparent interest in doing so. (After having read All-Star Batman and Robin, I think that's a good thing.) It essentially picks up right where Year One left off. Batman is still kind of new to all of this, still working out his code of ethics and how best to use the Batman persona. It's also a passing of the torch for Gotham itself, moving the city from one ruled by the mafia to one terrorized on a pr</span>
  <span id="freeText13240873027633303724" style="display:none">The Long Halloween is a follow-up to Year One, written by Jeph Loeb because Frank Miller had no apparent interest in doing so. (After having read All-Star Batman and Robin, I think that's a good thing.) It essentially picks up right where Year One left off. Batman is still kind of new to all of this, still working out his code of ethics and how best to use the Batman persona. It's also a passing of the torch for Gotham itself, moving the city from one ruled by the mafia to one terrorized on a pretty frequent basis by nutjobs in masks. I have to wonder what the average Gothamite would think about all this, and if they'd rather have Falcone or the Joker. It's also a detailed origin story of Two-Face. It sounds like a lot going on, but there's plenty of space in 13 issues to cover it all.<br /><br />Everything in the first paragraph is actually secondary to the real story, a mystery revolving around a serial killer dubbed Holiday because s/he kills only on holidays, leaving behind a token related to the day. It's a really, really good mystery. It's entirely engrossing, and the resolution is surprising and satisfying.<br /><br />My only issue with the book is that Tim Sale's art just doesn't work for me. Never has, and I doubt it ever will. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13240873027633303724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1726084813" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1726084813" />
    <a title="Sud666" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666"><img alt="Sud666" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418437112p2/36890366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1726084813?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sud666" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sud666" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666">Sud666</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1726084813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1342612466455985370">An utterly magnificent Batman tale. That is the best way I can describe this amazing story written by Jeph Loeb. If you love Batman or just appreciate a well crafted murder mystery then this is a book you will appreciate. The best part is the wonderful story is supplemented by Tim Sale's gorgeous art. This is a stylish volume. Beautifully illustrated with many memorable scenes.<br/><br/>The Long Halloween is a detective story centering around three distinct protagonists and a large cast of secondary chara</span>
  <span id="freeText1342612466455985370" style="display:none">An utterly magnificent Batman tale. That is the best way I can describe this amazing story written by Jeph Loeb. If you love Batman or just appreciate a well crafted murder mystery then this is a book you will appreciate. The best part is the wonderful story is supplemented by Tim Sale's gorgeous art. This is a stylish volume. Beautifully illustrated with many memorable scenes.<br /><br />The Long Halloween is a detective story centering around three distinct protagonists and a large cast of secondary characters. The three primary characters are Batman, Harvey Dent and Carmine Falcone. The story takes place in the very early days of Batman. Carmine Falcone is the undisputed head of the Gotham Crime world. Harvey Dent is the District Attorney that is obsessed with breaking up his criminal empire. Batman is well..Batman. The secondary cast of characters is vast. Many of Batman's Arkham foes make appearances in this tale. From Scarecrow and Joker to the Riddler and Mad Hatter. The relationship between Catwoman and Batman is also explored.<br /><br />A killer known as Holiday is gunning down various members of the mob. The question is who is Holiday? The beauty of this tale is that it hides the answer from you till the very end. I can honestly say I never saw the end coming. Very impressive. The candidates for Holiday are many from Carmine Falcone to Gigante Falcone, his rather brobdingnagian daughter, to Harvey Dent. To just approach this story from the detective aspects alone make this a worthwhile read. If you can unwrap the complete mystery of the Holiday killer than congratulations, because I could not till the end.<br /><br />This is also a Harvey Dent story. It has a very interesting origin story for Harvey. In many ways it is similar to the canon origin. But the depth afforded to Harvey's character is amazing. We see a driven and obsessive DA who clearly despises Falcone and his perversion of justice. But the story behind where he got the coin and his rationale for being Two-Face are excellent. Mr. Loeb nailed it.<br /><br />Mr. Loeb also is spot on with his myriad villains. I enjoyed that this complex detective story was still able to enmesh a plethora of Batman foes. I enjoyed seeing him deal with Poison Ivy and the Calendar Man. None of the appearances felt forced and were a vital part of the plot. At one point Catwoman is also a suspect in the killings.<br /><br />The artwork is amazing all throughout this book. The dark but vibrant colors do wonders not only for Batman, but for Gotham City and all his foes. The best part is it completely fits the somber atmosphere of this grim tale, but at points when the events soar to epic heights and grand confrontations the art follows in tandem with gorgeous scenes and full page illustrations. This is impressive talent on display. Enjoy it.<br /><br />At the end of the day, I would call The Long Halloween the quintessential Batman tale. We see him as a hero, a detective, a loyal friend and as a driven man trying to rid Gotham of the scourge of crime. I would highly recommend this to anyone. But it would be criminal for Batman fans to not read this and add it to their collection of all time favorite Batman tales. This is an instant classic. Loved it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1342612466455985370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TMVm7N7ZpsCc/L2hJn29xRUoxJjiUbnmeWYiMtwa+5ZiC0RyCMy0RAeu+RSZ4veUhH86Ia/c9J5ZVH5k3MVZoA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IqCpkHWnx1BzMwBLmaVmCpJK3tvWWRMwsp6K80Idk0wMbosOo7LV1OhhRP4mOixbAx0gYpvUXkiSrNalQsIxeg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer695955461075320855">Joseph "Jeph" Loeb III is an Emmy and WGA nominated American film and television writer, producer and award-winning comic book writer. Loeb was a Co-Executive Producer on the NBC hit show <i>Heroes</i>, and formerly a producer/writer on the TV series <i>Smallville</i> and <i>Lost</i>.<br/><br/>A four-time Eisner Award winner and five-time Wizard Fan Awards winner (see below), Loeb's comic book career includes work on many major</span>
  <span id="freeText695955461075320855" style="display:none">Joseph "Jeph" Loeb III is an Emmy and WGA nominated American film and television writer, producer and award-winning comic book writer. Loeb was a Co-Executive Producer on the NBC hit show <i>Heroes</i>, and formerly a producer/writer on the TV series <i>Smallville</i> and <i>Lost</i>.<br /><br />A four-time Eisner Award winner and five-time Wizard Fan Awards winner (see below), Loeb's comic book career includes work on many major characters, including Spider-Man, Batman, Superman, Hulk, Captain America, Cable, Iron Man, Daredevil, Supergirl, the Avengers, and Buffy the Vampire Slayer, much of which he has produced in collaboration with artist Tim Sale, who provides the comic art seen on <i>Heroes</i>.<br /></span>
